      <p><b>Kyrgyzstan</b>,<sup class="reference" id="ref_note_a1"><a href="#endnote_note_a1">[A]</a></sup> officially the <b>Kyrgyz Republic</b>,<sup class="reference" id="ref_note_b1"><a href="#endnote_note_b1">[B]</a></sup> also known as <b>Kirghizia</b> (in Russian),<sup class="reference" id="ref_note_c1"><a href="#endnote_note_c1">[C]</a></sup> is a landlocked country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="List of cities in Kyrgyzstan">largest city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>. </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan's history spans a variety of cultures and empires. Although geographically isolated by its highly mountainous terrain, Kyrgyzstan has been at the crossroads of several great civilizations as part of the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> and other commercial routes. Inhabited by a succession of tribes and clans, Kyrgyzstan has periodically fallen under larger domination. Between periods of self-government it was ruled by <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6kt%C3%BCrks" title="GÃ¶ktÃ¼rks">GÃ¶ktÃ¼rks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Khaganate" title="Uyghur Khaganate">Uyghur Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Khitan_people" title="Khitan people">Khitan people</a>, before being conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a> in the 13th century; it regained independence but was invaded by <a href="/wiki/Kalmyks" title="Kalmyks">Kalmyks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a>. In 1876, it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, remaining in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a> as the Kirghiz Soviet Socialist Republic after the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>. Following <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>'s democratic reforms in the USSR, in 1990 pro-independence candidate <a href="/wiki/Askar_Akayev" title="Askar Akayev">Askar Akayev</a> was elected president. On 31 August 1991, Kyrgyzstan declared independence from Moscow and a democratic government was established. Kyrgyzstan attained sovereignty as a nation state after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">breakup of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. </p>
      <p>Since independence, Kyrgyzstan has officially been a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential republic</a>, then between 2010 and 2021 a de jure a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, although de facto it had an executive President and was governed as a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi presidential</a> republic before reverting to a presidential system in 2021. it continues to endure ethnic conflicts,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> revolts,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> economic troubles,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> transitional governments<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and political conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ethnic <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a> make up the majority of the country's six million people, followed by significant minorities of <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a> is closely related to other <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic languages</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> remains spoken and is an official language, a legacy of a century of <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a>. 90% of the population are Muslims with the majority being <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-18">[18]</a></sup> In addition to its Turkic origins, Kyrgyz culture bears elements of Iranic, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolian</a> and Russian influence. </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">Eurasian Economic Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organization" title="Collective Security Treaty Organization">Collective Security Treaty Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">Turkic Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrksoy" class="mw-redirect" title="TÃ¼rksoy">TÃ¼rksoy</a> community and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> ranked 120th in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, and the second poorest country in Central Asia. The country's <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">transition economy</a> is heavily dependent on <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> along with deposits of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>. </p>
