      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><i>Kyrgyz</i> is believed to have been derived from the Turkic word for "forty", about the forty clans of <a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Manas" title="Epic of Manas">Manas</a>, a legendary hero who united forty regional clans against the <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Khaganate" title="Uyghur Khaganate">Uyghurs</a>. Literally, Kyrgyz means "We are forty". At the time, in the early 9th century AD, the Uyghurs dominated much of Central Asia (including Kyrgyzstan), Mongolia, and parts of modern-day Russia and China.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/-stan" title="-stan">-stan</a></i> is a word in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian language</a> meaning "place of" or "country". </p>
      <p>The 40-ray sun on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Flag of Kyrgyzstan">flag of Kyrgyzstan</a> is a reference to those same forty tribes and the graphical element in the sun's center depicts the wooden crown, called tunduk, of a <a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">yurt</a>âa portable dwelling traditionally used by nomads in the steppes of Central Asia. </p>
      <p>In terms of naming conventions, the country's official name is <i>"Kyrgyz Republic"</i> whenever it is used in some international arenas and foreign relations.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> However, in the English-speaking world, the spelling <i>Kyrgyzstan</i> is commonly used while its former name <i>Kirghizia</i> is rarely used as such.<sup id="cite_ref-Kirghizia_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirghizia-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="History of Kyrgyzstan">History of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png/220px-G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png/330px-G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png/440px-G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png 2x" data-file-width="1644" data-file-height="959"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6kturksAD551-572.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/First_Turkic_Khaganate" title="First Turkic Khaganate">First Turkic Khaganate</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to David C. King, <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> were early settlers in present-day Kyrgyzstan.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a> state reached its greatest expansion after defeating the <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyghur Empire">Uyghur</a> Khaganate in 840 AD.<sup id="cite_ref-Kyrgyzstan_timeline_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kyrgyzstan_timeline-24">[24]</a></sup> From the 10th century the Kyrgyz migrated as far as the <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> range and maintained their dominance over this territory for about 200 years. </p>
      <p>In the 12th century the Kyrgyz dominion had shrunk to the <a href="/wiki/Altay_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Altay Mountains">Altay</a> Range and <a href="/wiki/Sayan_Mountains" title="Sayan Mountains">Sayan Mountains</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Mongols_before_Genghis_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongols before Genghis Khan">Mongol expansion</a>. With the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> in the thirteenth century, the Kyrgyz migrated south. The Kyrgyz peacefully became a part of the Mongol Empire in 1207. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Issyk Kul Lake">Issyk Kul Lake</a> was a stopover on the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, a land route for traders, merchants, and other travelers from the Far East to Europe. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg/170px-Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg/255px-Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg/340px-Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caravanserai_Tash_Rabat_on_Silk_Road_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Silk_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Silk road">Silk road</a> <a href="/wiki/Caravansarai" class="mw-redirect" title="Caravansarai">caravansarai</a> utilized during the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyz tribes were overrun in the 17th century by the Mongols, in the mid-18th century by the Manchurian <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>, and in the early 19th century by the Uzbek <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">Khanate of Kokand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_conquest">Russian conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Russian conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the late nineteenth century, the eastern part of what is today Kyrgyzstan, mainly the <a href="/wiki/Issyk-Kul_Region" title="Issyk-Kul Region">Issyk-Kul Region</a>, was ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> by Qing China through the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tarbagatai" title="Treaty of Tarbagatai">Treaty of Tarbagatai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The territory, then known in Russian as "Kirghizia", was formally incorporated into the Empire in 1876. The Russian takeover was met with numerous revolts, and many of the Kyrgyz opted to relocate to the <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. </p>
      <p>In addition, the suppression of the <a href="/wiki/Urkun" class="mw-redirect" title="Urkun">1916 rebellion</a> against Russian rule in Central Asia caused many Kyrgyz later to migrate to China.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Since many ethnic groups in the region were (and still are) split between neighboring states at a time when borders were more porous and less regulated, it was common to move back and forth over the mountains, depending on where life was perceived as better; this might mean better rains for pasture or better government during oppression. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Kyrgyzstan">Soviet Kyrgyzstan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Soviet Kyrgyzstan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bischkek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Bischkek.jpg/220px-Bischkek.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Bischkek.jpg/330px-Bischkek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Bischkek.jpg/440px-Bischkek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="275"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bischkek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Soviet power was initially established in the region in 1919, and the <a href="/wiki/Kara-Kyrgyz_Autonomous_Oblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara-Kyrgyz Autonomous Oblast">Kara-Kyrgyz Autonomous Oblast</a> was created within the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a> (the phrase Kara-Kirghiz was used until the mid-1920s by the Russians to distinguish them from the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakhs</a>, who were also referred to as Kirghiz). On 5 December 1936, the <a href="/wiki/Kirghiz_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kirghiz Soviet Socialist Republic">Kirghiz Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was established as a constituent <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Union Republic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. </p>
      <p>During the 1920s, Kyrgyzstan developed considerably in cultural, educational, and social life. Literacy was greatly improved, and a standard literary language was introduced by imposing Russian on the populace. Economic and social development also was notable. Many aspects of the Kyrgyz national culture were retained despite the suppression of nationalist activity under <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>. </p>
      <p>The early years of <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a> had little effect on the political climate in Kyrgyzstan. However, the Republic's press was permitted to adopt a more liberal stance and to establish a new publication, <i>Literaturny Kirghizstan</i>, by the Union of Writers. Unofficial political groups were forbidden, but several groups that emerged in 1989 to deal with the acute housing crisis were permitted to function. </p>
      <p>According to the last Soviet census in 1989, ethnic Kyrgyz made up only 22% of the residents of the northern city of <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Frunze</a> (now Bishkek), while more than 60% were Russians, Ukrainians, and people from other <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> nations. Nearly 10% of the capital's population were Jewish (a rather unique fact, for almost any place in the Soviet Union, except the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Jewish Autonomous Oblast">Jewish Autonomous Oblast</a>). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan,_2011-05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan%2C_2011-05.jpg/220px-Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan%2C_2011-05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan%2C_2011-05.jpg/330px-Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan%2C_2011-05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan%2C_2011-05.jpg/440px-Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan%2C_2011-05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="945" data-file-height="709"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Kyrgyzstan,_2011-05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Urial" title="Urial">Urial</a> on a Kyrgyzstan stamp
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In June 1990, ethnic tensions between <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> and Kyrgyz surfaced in the <a href="/wiki/Osh_Oblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Osh Oblast">Osh Oblast</a> (southern Kyrgyzstan), where Uzbeks form a minority of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-conflict_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conflict-28">[28]</a></sup> The tensions between Kyrgyzs and Uzbeks in Osis led to 186 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Attempts to appropriate Uzbek <a href="/wiki/Collective_farming" title="Collective farming">collective farms</a> for housing development triggered the <a href="/wiki/Osh_riots_(1990)" title="Osh riots (1990)">Osh Riots</a>. A state of emergency and curfew were introduced<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Askar_Akayev" title="Askar Akayev">Askar Akayev</a>, the youngest of five sons born into a family of collective farm workers (in northern Kyrgyzstan), was elected president in October of that same year. By then, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Movement_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Democratic Movement of Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan Democratic Movement</a> (KDM) had developed into a significant political force with support in Parliament. On 15 December 1990, the Supreme Soviet voted to change the republic's name to the Republic of Kyrgyzstan. The following January, Akayev introduced new government structures and appointed a new cabinet composed mainly of younger, reform-oriented politicians. In February 1991, the name of the capital, Frunze, was changed back to its pre-revolutionary name of Bishkek.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite these political moves toward independence, economic realities seemed to work against secession from the Soviet Union. In a referendum on the preservation of the Soviet Union in March 1991, 88.7% of the voters approved the proposal to retain the Soviet Union as a "renewed federation". Nevertheless, secessionist forces pushed Kyrgyzstan's independence through in August of that same year. </p>
      <p>On 19 August 1991, when the <a href="/wiki/State_Committee_on_the_State_of_Emergency" title="State Committee on the State of Emergency">State Emergency Committee</a> assumed power in Moscow, there was an attempt to depose Akayev in Kyrgyzstan. After the coup collapsed the following week, Akayev and Vice President <a href="/wiki/German_Kuznetsov" title="German Kuznetsov">German Kuznetsov</a> announced their resignations from the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a> (CPSU), and the entire bureau and secretariat resigned. This was followed by the Supreme Soviet vote declaring independence from the Soviet Union on 31 August 1991 as the <b>Republic of Kyrgyzstan</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In October 1991, Akayev ran unopposed and was elected president of the new independent Republic by direct ballot, receiving 95 percent of the votes cast. Together with the representatives of seven other Republics that same month, he signed the Treaty of the New Economic Community. Finally, on 21 December 1991, Kyrgyzstan joined with the other four Central Asian Republics to formally enter the new <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>. Kyrgyzstan gained full independence a few days later on 25 December 1991. The following day, on 26 December 1991, the Soviet Union ceased to exist. In 1992, Kyrgyzstan joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE). On 5 May 1993, the official name changed from the Republic of Kyrgyzstan to the Kyrgyz Republic. </p>
      <p>In 2005, a popular uprising known as the "<a href="/wiki/Tulip_Revolution" title="Tulip Revolution">Tulip Revolution</a>", took place after the parliamentary elections in March 2005, forced President <a href="/wiki/Askar_Akayev" title="Askar Akayev">Askar Akayev</a>'s resignation on 4 April 2005. Opposition leaders formed a coalition, and a new government was formed under President <a href="/wiki/Kurmanbek_Bakiyev" title="Kurmanbek Bakiyev">Kurmanbek Bakiyev</a> and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Feliks_Kulov" class="mw-redirect" title="Feliks Kulov">Feliks Kulov</a>. The nation's capital was looted during the protests. </p>
      <p>Political stability appeared to be elusive, however, as various groups and factions allegedly linked to <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">organized crime</a> jockeyed for power. Three of the 75 members of Parliament elected in March 2005 were assassinated, and another member was assassinated on 10 May 2006 shortly after winning his murdered brother's seat in a by-election. All four are reputed to have been directly involved in major illegal business ventures.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (December 2014)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> On 6 April 2010, <a href="/wiki/2010_Kyrgyzstan_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Kyrgyzstan revolution">civil unrest broke out</a> in the town of <a href="/wiki/Talas,_Kyrgyzstan" title="Talas, Kyrgyzstan">Talas</a> after a demonstration against government corruption and increased living expenses. The protests became violent, spreading to Bishkek by the following day. Protesters attacked President Bakiyev's offices, as well as state-run radio and television stations. There were conflicting reports that Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Moldomusa_Kongatiyev" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldomusa Kongatiyev">Moldomusa Kongatiyev</a> had been beaten. On 7 April 2010, President Bakiyev imposed a state of emergency. Police and special services arrested many opposition leaders. In response, protesters took control of the internal security headquarters (former <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a> headquarters) and a state television channel in the capital, Bishkek.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Reports by Kyrgyzstan government officials indicated that at least 75 people were killed and 458 hospitalized in bloody clashes with police in the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Reports say that at least 80 people died as a result of clashes with police. A transition government, led by former foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Roza_Otunbayeva" title="Roza Otunbayeva">Roza Otunbayeva</a>, by 8 April 2010 had taken control of <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Kyrgyzstan">state media</a> and government facilities in the capital, but Bakiyev had not resigned from office.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>President Bakiyev returned to his home in <a href="/wiki/Jalal-Abad" title="Jalal-Abad">Jalal-Abad</a> and stated his terms of resignation at a press conference on 13 April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> On 15 April 2010, Bakiyev left the country and flew to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, along with his wife and two children. The country's provisional leaders announced that Bakiyev signed a formal letter of resignation prior to his departure.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Daniar_Usenov" title="Daniar Usenov">Daniar Usenov</a> accused Russia of supporting the protests; this accusation was denied by Russian Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>. Opposition members also called for the closing of the US-controlled <a href="/wiki/Manas_Air_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Manas Air Base">Manas Air Base</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Russia's President <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> ordered measures to ensure the safety of Russian nationals and tighten security around Russian sites in Kyrgyzstan to protect them against possible attacks. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_South_Kyrgyzstan_ethnic_clashes" title="2010 South Kyrgyzstan ethnic clashes">2010 South Kyrgyzstan ethnic clashes</a> occurred between the two main ethnic groupsâthe Uzbeks and Kyrgyzâin <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a>, the second-largest city in the country, on 11 June 2010. The clashes incited fears that the country could be heading towards a civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Suusamyr_Valley_(3968060227).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Suusamyr_Valley_%283968060227%29.jpg/220px-Suusamyr_Valley_%283968060227%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Suusamyr_Valley_%283968060227%29.jpg/330px-Suusamyr_Valley_%283968060227%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Suusamyr_Valley_%283968060227%29.jpg/440px-Suusamyr_Valley_%283968060227%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="749"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Suusamyr_Valley_(3968060227).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nomads in Kyrgyzstan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Finding it difficult to control the situation, Otunbayeva, the interim leader, sent a letter to the Russian president, Dimitry Medvedev, asking him to send Russian troops to help the country control the situation. Medvedev's Press AttachÃ©, <a href="/wiki/Natalya_Timakova" title="Natalya Timakova">Natalya Timakova</a>, said in a reply to the letter, "It is an internal conflict and for now Russia does not see the conditions for taking part in its resolution". The clashes caused a shortage of food and other essential commodities with more than 200 killed and 1,685 people hurt, as of 12&nbsp;June&nbsp;2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. The Russian government, however, said it would be sending humanitarian aid to the troubled nation.<sup id="cite_ref-By2010_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-By2010-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to local sources, there was a clash between two local gangs and it did not take long for the violence to spread to the rest of the city. There were also reports that the armed forces supported ethnic Kyrgyz gangs entering the city, but the government denied the allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-By2010_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-By2010-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The riots spread to neighboring areas, and the government declared a state of emergency in the entire southern <a href="/wiki/Jalal-Abad" title="Jalal-Abad">Jalal-Abad</a> region. To control the situation, the interim government gave special shoot-to-kill powers to the security forces. The Russian government decided to send a battalion to the country to protect Russian facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-By_the_BBC_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-By_the_BBC-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg/220px-Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg/330px-Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg/440px-Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1019" data-file-height="693"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyz_family_Sary-Mogol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kyrgyz family in the village of Sary-Mogol, <a href="/wiki/Osh_Region" title="Osh Region">Osh Region</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Otunbayeva accused the family of Bakiyev of "instigating the riots".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> AFP reported "a veil of smoke covering the whole city". Authorities in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> said at least 30,000 Uzbeks had crossed the border to escape the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-By_the_BBC_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-By_the_BBC-42">[42]</a></sup> Osh became relatively calm on 14 June 2010, but Jalal-Abad witnessed sporadic incidents of arson. The entire region was still under a state of emergency as Uzbeks were reluctant to leave their houses for fear of attacks by the mobs. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> decided to send an envoy to assess the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh,_Kyrgyzstan_(43654601644).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh%2C_Kyrgyzstan_%2843654601644%29.jpg/220px-From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh%2C_Kyrgyzstan_%2843654601644%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh%2C_Kyrgyzstan_%2843654601644%29.jpg/330px-From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh%2C_Kyrgyzstan_%2843654601644%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh%2C_Kyrgyzstan_%2843654601644%29.jpg/440px-From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh%2C_Kyrgyzstan_%2843654601644%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3194" data-file-height="2192"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:From_Sary_Tash_to_Osh,_Kyrgyzstan_(43654601644).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kyrgyzstan's second-largest city, <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a>, in 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Temir_Sariyev" title="Temir Sariyev">Temir Sariyev</a>, deputy chief of the interim government, said there were local clashes and that it was not possible [for the government] to fully control the situation. He added that there were not sufficient security forces to contain the violence. Media agencies reported on 14 June 2010 that the Russian government was considering a request by the Kyrgyz government. An emergency meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">Collective Security Treaty Organisation</a> (CSTO) was held on the same day (14 June) to discuss the role it could play in helping to end the violence. Ethnic violence waned, according to the Kyrgyz government, by 15 June 2010 and Kyrgyz president Roza Otunbayeva held a news conference that day and declared that there was no need for Russia to send in troops to quell the violence. There were at least 170 people left dead by 15 June 2010 but Pascale Meige Wagner of the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a> said the [official] death toll was an underestimate. The UN High Commissioner told reporters in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> that evidence suggested that the violence seemed to have been staged up. Ethnic Uzbeks threatened to blow up an oil depot in Osh if they failed to get guarantees of protection. The United Nations said it believed that the attacks were "orchestrated, targeted and well-planned". Kyrgyz officials told the media that a person suspected to be behind the violence in Jalal-Abad had been detained.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_2010-06-16_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_2010-06-16-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 2 August 2010, a Kyrgyz government commission began investigating the causes of the clashes. Members of the National Commission, led by former parliament speaker Abdygany Erkebaev, met with people from the predominantly ethnic Uzbek villages of Mady, Shark, and Kyzyl-Kyshtak in the Kara-Suu district of Osh Oblast. This National Commission, including representatives of many ethnic groups, was established by a presidential decree. </p>
      <p>President Roza Otunbayeva also said in August 2010 that an international commission would be formed to investigate the clashes.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The international commission conducted an extensive investigation and prepared a report â The Independent international commission of inquiry into the events in southern Kyrgyzstan in June 2010 (KIC).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> It stated that "The Provisional Government, which had assumed power two months before the events, either failed to recognize or underestimated the deterioration in inter-ethnic relations in southern Kyrgyzstan". The KIC concluded that the "Provisional Government had the responsibility to ensure that the security forces were adequately trained and appropriately equipped to deal with situations of civil unrest" but were unable to take necessary measures. </p>
      <p>As of today, Kyrgyzstan celebrates its Independence Day annually on August 31, the anniversary of its declaration of independence in 1991. Since independence, Kyrgyzstan has made some impressive developments such as creating genuinely free news media and fostering an active political opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Geography of Kyrgyzstan">Geography of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png/220px-Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png/330px-Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png/440px-Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="1705" data-file-height="1015"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyzstan_Topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kyrgyzstan's topography
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bringing_the_sheep_home,_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_(3968109583).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bringing_the_sheep_home%2C_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_%283968109583%29.jpg/220px-Bringing_the_sheep_home%2C_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_%283968109583%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bringing_the_sheep_home%2C_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_%283968109583%29.jpg/330px-Bringing_the_sheep_home%2C_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_%283968109583%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Bringing_the_sheep_home%2C_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_%283968109583%29.jpg/440px-Bringing_the_sheep_home%2C_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issyk-Kul_%283968109583%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bringing_the_sheep_home,_on_the_southern_shore_of_Issy-Kol._(3968109583).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>On the southern shore of Issyk Kul lake, <a href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Issyk Kul Region">Issyk Kul Region</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is a landlocked country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, bordering <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, China, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/39th_parallel_north" title="39th parallel north">39Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_parallel_north" title="44th parallel north">44Â° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/69th_meridian_east" title="69th meridian east">69Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/81st_meridian_east" title="81st meridian east">81Â° E</a>. It is farther from the sea than any other individual country, and all its rivers flow into <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">closed drainage systems which do not reach the sea</a>. The mountainous region of the <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> covers over 80% of the country (Kyrgyzstan is occasionally referred to as "the Switzerland of Central Asia", as a result),<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> with the remainder made up of valleys and basins. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyzstan.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Kyrgyzstan.png/330px-Kyrgyzstan.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Kyrgyzstan.png/495px-Kyrgyzstan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/Kyrgyzstan.png 2x" data-file-width="633" data-file-height="321"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyzstan.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Kyrgyzstan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Issyk-Kul_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Issyk-Kul Lake">Issyk-Kul Lake</a>, or Ysyk-KÃ¶l in <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyrgyz Language">Kyrgyz</a>, in the north-eastern Tian Shan is the largest lake in Kyrgyzstan and the second largest mountain lake in the world after <a href="/wiki/Titicaca" class="mw-redirect" title="Titicaca">Titicaca</a>. The lowest point is in <a href="/wiki/Kara_Darya" title="Kara Darya">Kara-Daryya</a> (Karadar'ya) at 132 meters and the highest peaks are in the Kakshaal-Too range, forming the Chinese border. Peak <a href="/wiki/Jengish_Chokusu" title="Jengish Chokusu">Jengish Chokusu</a>, at 7,439&nbsp;m (24,406&nbsp;ft), is the highest point and is considered by geologists to be the northernmost peak over 7,000&nbsp;m (22,966&nbsp;ft) in the world. Heavy snowfall in winter leads to spring floods which often cause serious damage downstream. The runoff from the mountains is also used for <a href="/wiki/Hydro-electricity" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydro-electricity">hydro-electricity</a>. </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan has significant deposits of metals including <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rare-earth_metals" class="mw-redirect" title="Rare-earth metals">rare-earth metals</a>. Due to the country's predominantly mountainous terrain, less than 8% of the land is cultivated, and this is concentrated in the northern lowlands and the fringes of the <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana Valley</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> in the north is the capital and largest city, with 937,400 inhabitants (as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>). The second city is the ancient town of <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a>, located in the Fergana Valley near the border with Uzbekistan. The principal river is the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Darya" title="Kara Darya">Kara Darya</a>, which flows west through the Fergana Valley into Uzbekistan. Across the border in Uzbekistan it meets another major Kyrgyz river, the <a href="/wiki/Naryn_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Naryn River">Naryn</a>. </p>
      <p>The confluence forms the <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syr Darya</a>, which originally flowed into the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>. As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it no longer reaches the sea, as its water is withdrawn upstream to irrigate cotton fields in <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, and southern <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chu_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Chu River">Chu River</a> also briefly flows through Kyrgyzstan before entering Kazakhstan. </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan contains seven terrestrial ecosystems: <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan_montane_conifer_forests" title="Tian Shan montane conifer forests">Tian Shan montane conifer forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alai-Western_Tian_Shan_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Alai-Western Tian Shan steppe">Alai-Western Tian Shan steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gissaro-Alai_open_woodlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Gissaro-Alai open woodlands">Gissaro-Alai open woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan_foothill_arid_steppe" title="Tian Shan foothill arid steppe">Tian Shan foothill arid steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamir_alpine_desert_and_tundra" title="Pamir alpine desert and tundra">Pamir alpine desert and tundra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan_montane_steppe_and_meadows" title="Tian Shan montane steppe and meadows">Tian Shan montane steppe and meadows</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_northern_desert" title="Central Asian northern desert">Central Asian northern desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-50">[50]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.86/10, ranking it 13th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg/310px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg/465px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg/620px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1769" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_KGZ_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kyrgyzstan map of KÃ¶ppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Kyrgyzstan">Climate of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate varies regionally. The low-lying <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana Valley</a> in the southwest is <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical</a> and extremely hot in <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summer</a>, with temperatures reaching 40&nbsp;Â°C (104&nbsp;Â°F) The northern <a href="/wiki/Foothill" class="mw-redirect" title="Foothill">foothills</a> are <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> varies from dry <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a> to <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">polar climate</a>, depending on elevation. In the coldest areas temperatures are sub-zero for around 40 days in winter, and even some <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> areas experience constant snowfall in this period. In the lowlands the temperature ranges from around â6&nbsp;Â°C (21&nbsp;Â°F) in January to 24&nbsp;Â°C (75&nbsp;Â°F) in July. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Climate change in Kyrgyzstan">Climate change in Kyrgyzstan</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Climate change in Kyrgyzstan">Climate change in Kyrgyzstan</a> is already having impacts. Among the countries in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, Kyrgyzstan is the third most vulnerable to the <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">effects of climate change</a>, such as changes in weather patterns that could lead to prolonged periods of precipitation and drought.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Their average temperature has increased from 5.8&nbsp;Â°C to 6&nbsp;Â°C so far within the last 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan_:22_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan_:22-53">[53]</a></sup> By 2060, there is an expectation of a 0.2&nbsp;Â°C increase in average mean temperature, as well as a 0.3&nbsp;Â°C increase by 2100.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan_:14_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Kyrgyzstan_:14-54">[54]</a></sup> However the very slight increase in temperature is expected to positively affect climate-sensitive sectors such as agriculture, energy, and forestry as more land is within the optimum temperature band.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enclaves_and_exclaves">Enclaves and exclaves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Enclaves and exclaves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There is one <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a>, the tiny village of <a href="/wiki/Barak,_Kyrgyzstan" title="Barak, Kyrgyzstan">Barak</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> (population 627), in the <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana Valley</a>. The village is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbek</a> territory. It is located on the road from <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a> (Kyrgyzstan) to Khodjaabad (Uzbekistan) about 4 kilometres (2 miles) north-west from the KyrgyzâUzbek border in the direction of <a href="/wiki/Andijan" title="Andijan">Andijan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Barak is administratively part of <a href="/wiki/Kara-Suu_District" title="Kara-Suu District">Kara-Suu District</a> in Kyrgyzstan's <a href="/wiki/Osh_Region" title="Osh Region">Osh Region</a>. </p>
      <p>There are four Uzbek <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclaves</a> within Kyrgyzstan. Two of them are the towns of <a href="/wiki/Sokh_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Sokh District">Sokh</a>, with an area of 325&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (125&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and a population of 42,800 in 1993âalthough some estimates go as high as 70,000 (99% are <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik people">Tajiks</a>, the remainder <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Shohimardon" title="Shohimardon">Shakhimardan</a> (also known as Shahimardan, Shohimardon, or Shah-i-Mardan, area 90&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (35&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and a population of 5,100 in 1993; 91% are Uzbeks, the remainder <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a>); the other two are the tiny territories of Chong-Kara (roughly 3&nbsp;km (2&nbsp;mi) long by 1&nbsp;km (0.6&nbsp;mi) wide) and Jangy-ayyl (a dot of land barely 2â3&nbsp;km (1â2&nbsp;mi) across). Chong-Kara is on the <a href="/wiki/Sokh_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Sokh river">Sokh river</a>, between the Uzbek border and the Sokh enclave. Jangy-ayyl is about 60 kilometres (37&nbsp;mi) east of <a href="/wiki/Batken" title="Batken">Batken</a>, in a northward projection of the Kyrgyz-Uzbek border near <a href="/wiki/Khalmion" title="Khalmion">Khalmion</a>. </p>
      <p>There are also two enclaves belonging to <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>: <a href="/wiki/Vorukh" title="Vorukh">Vorukh</a> (exclave area between 95â130&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (37â50&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), population estimated between 23,000 and 29,000, 95% Tajiks and 5% Kyrgyz, distributed among 17 villages), located 45 kilometres (28&nbsp;mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Isfara" title="Isfara">Isfara</a> on the right bank of the Karafshin river, and a small settlement near the Kyrgyz railway station of <a href="/wiki/Kairagach" class="mw-redirect" title="Kairagach">Kairagach</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Kyrgyzstan">Government of Kyrgyzstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Politics of Kyrgyzstan">Politics of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">Political system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:190px;max-width:190px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:251px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_(2018-05-14)_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sooronbay Jeenbekov" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg/188px-Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="188" height="251" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg/282px-Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg/376px-Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="1037"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Sooronbay_Jeenbekov" title="Sooronbay Jeenbekov">Sooronbay Jeenbekov</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="President of Kyrgyzstan">President</a>, in office from 2017 to 2020.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%932010_Constitution_of_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="1993â2010 Constitution of Kyrgyzstan">1993 constitution</a> defines the form of government as a democratic <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> republic. The executive branch includes a president and prime minister. The parliament currently is unicameral. The judicial branch comprises a Supreme Court, local courts and a Chief Prosecutor. </p>
      <p>In March 2002, in the southern district of <a href="/wiki/Aksy" class="mw-redirect" title="Aksy">Aksy</a>, five people protesting the <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest_and_detention" title="Arbitrary arrest and detention">arbitrary arrest</a> of an opposition politician were shot dead by police, sparking nationwide protests. President <a href="/wiki/Askar_Akayev" title="Askar Akayev">Askar Akayev</a> initiated a constitutional reform process which initially included the participation of a broad range of government, civil and social representatives in an open dialogue, leading to a February 2003 referendum marred by voting irregularities. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bishkek_P9170503_192_(39204123095).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bishkek_P9170503_192_%2839204123095%29.jpg/220px-Bishkek_P9170503_192_%2839204123095%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bishkek_P9170503_192_%2839204123095%29.jpg/330px-Bishkek_P9170503_192_%2839204123095%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bishkek_P9170503_192_%2839204123095%29.jpg/440px-Bishkek_P9170503_192_%2839204123095%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bishkek_P9170503_192_(39204123095).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_(Kyrgyzstan)" title="Supreme Council (Kyrgyzstan)">Supreme Council</a> building in <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The amendments to the constitution approved by the referendum resulted in stronger control by the president and weakened the parliament and the Constitutional Court. Parliamentary elections for a new, 75-seat unicameral legislature were held on 27 February and 13 March 2005, but were widely viewed as corrupt. The subsequent protests led to a bloodless <a href="/wiki/Coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup">coup</a> on 24 March 2005, after which Akayev fled the country with his family and was replaced by acting president <a href="/wiki/Kurmanbek_Bakiyev" title="Kurmanbek Bakiyev">Kurmanbek Bakiyev</a> (see: <a href="/wiki/Tulip_Revolution" title="Tulip Revolution">Tulip Revolution</a>). </p>
      <p>On 10 July 2005, acting president Bakiyev won the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_presidential_election,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyrgyz presidential election, 2005">presidential election</a> in a landslide, with 88.9% of the vote, and was inaugurated on 14 August. However, initial public support for the new administration substantially declined in subsequent months as a result of its apparent inability to solve the corruption problems that had plagued the country since its independence from the Soviet Union, along with the murders of several members of parliament. Large-scale protests against president Bakiyev took place in Bishkek in April and November 2006, with opposition leaders accusing the president of failing to live up to his election promises to reform the country's constitution and transfer many of his presidential powers to parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_(2018-05-14)_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_01.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_01.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_01.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_%282018-05-14%29_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Sooronbay_Jeenbekov_(2018-05-14)_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Sooronbay_Jeenbekov" title="Sooronbay Jeenbekov">Sooronbay Jeenbekov</a> and Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, 14 May 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE), a league of 56 participating states committed to peace, transparency, and the protection of human rights in Eurasia. As an OSCE participating State, Kyrgyzstan's international commitments are subject to monitoring under the mandate of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Helsinki_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Helsinki Commission">U.S. Helsinki Commission</a>. </p>
      <p>In December 2008, the state-owned broadcast <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_Television" title="Kyrgyz Television">KTRK</a> announced that it would require prior submission of <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a> programmes, which KTRK are required to retransmit according to a 2005 agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> KTRK had stopped retransmitting RFE/RL programming in October 2008, a week after it failed to broadcast an RFE/RL programme called 'Inconvenient Questions' which covered the October elections, claiming to have lost the missing material. President Bakiyev had criticised this programme in September 2008, while KTRK told RFE/RL that its programming was too negative. <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, which ranks Kyrgyzstan 111th out of 173 countries on its <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a>, strongly criticised the decision. </p>
      <p>On 3 February 2009, President <a href="/wiki/Kurmanbek_Bakiyev" title="Kurmanbek Bakiyev">Kurmanbek Bakiyev</a> announced the imminent closure of the <a href="/wiki/Manas_Air_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Manas Air Base">Manas Air Base</a>, the only US military base remaining in Central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The closure was approved by Parliament on 19 February 2009 by a vote of 78â1 for the government-backed bill.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> However, after much behind-the-scenes negotiation between Kyrgyz, Russian and American diplomats, the decision was reversed in June 2009. The Americans were allowed to remain under a new contract, whereby rent would increase from $17.4 million to $60 million annually.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SCO_summit_(2018-06-10)_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/SCO_summit_%282018-06-10%29_7.jpg/220px-SCO_summit_%282018-06-10%29_7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/SCO_summit_%282018-06-10%29_7.jpg/330px-SCO_summit_%282018-06-10%29_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/SCO_summit_%282018-06-10%29_7.jpg/440px-SCO_summit_%282018-06-10%29_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SCO_summit_(2018-06-10)_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President Sooronbay Jeenbekov at the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a> summit in China, June 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is among the fifty countries in the world with the highest perceived level of corruption: the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perception_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Corruption Perception Index">Corruption Perception Index</a> for Kyrgyzstan is 28 on a scale of 0 (most corrupt) to 100 (least corrupt).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2010 another revolution erupted in the country (see: <a href="/wiki/2010_Kyrgyzstani_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Kyrgyzstani revolution">April uprising</a>). President Kurmanbek Bakiyev together with his relatives including his son <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Bakiyev" title="Maxim Bakiyev">Maksim</a><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and brother <a href="/wiki/Janish_Bakiyev" title="Janish Bakiyev">Janish</a>âwere forced to flee to Kazakhstan and then sought asylum in <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roza_Otunbayeva" title="Roza Otunbayeva">Roza Otunbayeva</a>, who was appointed interim president, announced that she did not intend to run for the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_presidential_election,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyrgyz presidential election, 2011">Presidential elections in 2011</a>. The election was held in November and won by the then-Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Almazbek_Atambayev" title="Almazbek Atambayev">Almazbek Atambayev</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Social Democratic Party of Kyrgyzstan">Social Democratic Party</a>, and Atambayev was sworn in as president on 1 December 2011. <a href="/wiki/Omurbek_Babanov" class="mw-redirect" title="Omurbek Babanov">Omurbek Babanov</a> was appointed prime minister on the same day and was confirmed on 23 December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2017, <a href="/wiki/Sooronbay_Jeenbekov" title="Sooronbay Jeenbekov">Sooronbay Jeenbekov</a>, a former prime minister backed by incumbent Almazbek Atambayev, was elected as the new President of Kyrgyzstan.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On 7 August 2019, the Special Forces of Kyrgyzstan launched an operation against the residence of former President Almazbek Atambayev, supposedly based on charges of corruption made against him.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In a meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Security_Council_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Security Council of Kyrgyzstan">Security Council</a>, President Jeenbekov accused Atambayev of violating the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In October 2020, President Sooronbay Jeenbekov resigned after protests caused by irregularities in parliamentary <a href="/wiki/2020_Kyrgyz_parliamentary_election" title="2020 Kyrgyz parliamentary election">elections</a> on 4 October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In January 2021, <a href="/wiki/Sadyr_Japarov" title="Sadyr Japarov">Sadyr Japarov</a> was elected as the new president after winning the presidential <a href="/wiki/2021_Kyrgyz_presidential_election" title="2021 Kyrgyz presidential election">election</a> by landslide.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2021, the majority of voters approved in the constitutional <a href="/wiki/2021_Kyrgyz_constitutional_referendum" title="2021 Kyrgyz constitutional referendum">referendum</a> a new constitution that will give new powers to the president, strengthening significantly presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG/220px-Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG/330px-Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG/440px-Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Multinational_forces_participate_in_Regional_Cooperation_12_Exercise_-06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kyrgyz soldiers conducting mine sweeping exercises.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Republic_of_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed Forces of the Republic of Kyrgyzstan">Armed Forces of the Republic of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The armed forces of Kyrgyzstan were formed after the <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Collapse of the Soviet Union">collapse of the Soviet Union</a> and consist of the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_Army" title="Kyrgyz Army">Land Forces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_Air_Force" title="Kyrgyz Air Force">Air Forces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internal_Troops_of_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal Troops of Kyrgyzstan">internal troops</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_(Kyrgyzstan)" title="National Guard (Kyrgyzstan)">National Guard</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan_Frontier_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyrgyzstan Frontier Force">border guard</a>. The military works with the <a href="/wiki/US_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="US Armed Forces">US Armed Forces</a>, which leased a facility named the <a href="/wiki/Transit_Center_at_Manas" title="Transit Center at Manas">Transit Center at Manas</a> at Manas International Airport near Bishkek until June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In recent years, the armed forces have begun developing better relations with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> including signing modernization deals worth $1.1bn and partaking in more exercises with Russian troops.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Agency_of_National_Security_(Kyrgyzstan)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Agency of National Security (Kyrgyzstan) (page does not exist)">Agency of National Security</a> works with the military and serves similar purposes to its Soviet predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a>. It oversees an elite counterterrorism special forces unit known as "Alfa", the same name used by other former Soviet countries, including <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>. The police are commanded by the Ministry of the Interior Affairs, along with the border guard.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Human rights in Kyrgyzstan">Human rights in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is classified as a "<a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a>, ranking 107th out of 167 for 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Kyrgyzstan was also ranked "not free" in the 2021 <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> report with a score of 28/100. In 2020, it was ranked "partly free" with a score of 39/100.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the installment of a more democratic government, many human rights violations still take place. While the country is performing well compared to other states in Central Asia, LGBT rights have been getting worse; but the freedom of press has been improving. </p>
      <p>In a move that alarmed human-rights groups, dozens of prominent Uzbek religious and community leaders were arrested by security forces following the <a href="/wiki/2010_South_Kyrgyzstan_ethnic_clashes" title="2010 South Kyrgyzstan ethnic clashes">2010 South Kyrgyzstan riots</a>, including journalist and human-rights activist <a href="/wiki/Azimzhan_Askarov" title="Azimzhan Askarov">Azimzhan Askarov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kramer_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kramer-77">[77]</a></sup> A law banning women under the age of 23 from traveling abroad without a parent or guardian, with the purpose of "increased morality and preservation of the gene pool" passed in the Kyrgyz parliament in June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> American diplomats expressed concern in October 2014 when Kyrgyzstan lawmakers passed a law that imposes jail terms on <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="LGBT rights in Kyrgyzstan">gay-rights activists</a> and others, including journalists, who create âa positive attitude toward non-traditional sexual relations.â<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstani activist and journalist Azimzhan Askarov was sentenced to life in prison in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On 24 January 2017, a Kyrgyz court has reinstated a sentence of life imprisonment for Askarov.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Regions of Kyrgyzstan">Regions of Kyrgyzstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Districts of Kyrgyzstan">Districts of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is divided into seven <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Regions of Kyrgyzstan">regions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>: <span lang="ky">Ð¾Ð±Ð»ÑÑÑÐ°Ñ</span>, <i lang="ky-Latn" title="Kyrgyz-language text">oblustar</i>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Ð¾Ð±Ð»Ð°ÑÑÐ¸</span>, <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">oblasti</i>). The regions are subdivided into 44 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Districts of Kyrgyzstan">districts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>: <span lang="ky">Ð°Ð¹Ð¼Ð°ÐºÑÐ°Ñ</span>, <i lang="ky-Latn" title="Kyrgyz-language text">aymaqtar</i>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">ÑÐ°Ð¹Ð¾Ð½Ñ</span>, <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">rayony</i>). The districts are further subdivided into rural districts at the lowest level of administration, which include all rural settlements (<i>ayÄ±l Ã¶kmÃ¶tÃ¼</i>) and villages without an associated municipal government. </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="special_status_cities"></span>The cities of <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a> have status "state importance" and do not belong to any region. </p>
      <p>Each region is headed by an akim (regional governor) appointed by the president. District akims [akimi?] are appointed by regional akims. </p> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 226px; width: 400px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_ea227c46d4e1f116"><area href="/wiki/Osh" shape="rect" coords="114,120,130,137" alt="Osh" title="Osh"><area href="/wiki/Bishkek" shape="rect" coords="209,10,224,25" alt="Bishkek" title="Bishkek"><area href="/wiki/Batken_Province" shape="rect" coords="51,166,75,186" alt="Batken Province" title="Batken Province"><area href="/wiki/Osh_Province" shape="rect" coords="141,150,161,171" alt="Osh Province" title="Osh Province"><area href="/wiki/Jalal-Abad_Province" shape="rect" coords="116,80,140,99" alt="Jalal-Abad Province" title="Jalal-Abad Province"><area href="/wiki/Naryn_Province" shape="rect" coords="213,89,240,109" alt="Naryn Province" title="Naryn Province"><area href="/wiki/Talas_Province" shape="rect" coords="107,37,128,58" alt="Talas Province" title="Talas Province"><area href="/wiki/Chuy_Province" shape="rect" coords="172,31,187,48" alt="Chuy Province" title="Chuy Province"><area href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul_Province" shape="rect" coords="297,53,318,73" alt="Issyk Kul Province" title="Issyk Kul Province"></map>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
