      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Economy of Kyrgyzstan">Economy of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyzstan_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Kyrgyzstan 's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_the_Kyrgyz_Republic" title="National Bank of the Kyrgyz Republic">National Bank of the Kyrgyz Republic</a> serves as the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> of Kyrgyzstan. </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan was the ninth poorest country in the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and is today the second poorest country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> after Tajikistan. 22.4% of the country's population lives below the poverty line.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite the backing of major Western lenders, including the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, Kyrgyzstan has had economic difficulties following independence. Initially, these were a result of the breakup of the Soviet trade bloc and resulting loss of markets, which impeded the republic's transition to a demand economy. </p>
      <p>The government has reduced expenditures, ended most price subsidies and introduced a <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">value-added tax</a>. Overall, the government appears committed to the transition to a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. Through economic stabilization and reform, the government seeks to establish a pattern of long-term consistent growth. Reforms led to Kyrgyzstan's accession to the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) on 20 December 1998. </p>
      <p>The Kyrgyz economy was severely affected by the collapse of the Soviet Union and the resulting loss of its vast market. In 1990, some 98% of Kyrgyz exports went to other parts of the Soviet Union. Thus, the nation's economic performance in the early 1990s was worse than any other former Soviet republic except war-torn <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, as factories and state farms collapsed with the disappearance of their traditional markets in the former Soviet Union. While economic performance has improved considerably in the last few years, and particularly since 1998, difficulties remain in securing adequate <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiscal Policy">fiscal</a> revenues and providing an adequate <a href="/wiki/Social_safety_net" title="Social safety net">social safety net</a>. <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">Remittances</a> of around 800,000 Kyrgyz migrants working in Russia represent 40% of Kyrgyzstan's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> is an important sector of the economy in Kyrgyzstan (see <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Agriculture in Kyrgyzstan">agriculture in Kyrgyzstan</a>). By the early 1990s, the private agricultural sector provided between one-third and one-half of some harvests. In 2002, agriculture accounted for 35.6% of GDP and about half of employment. Kyrgyzstan's terrain is mountainous, which accommodates <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> raising, the largest agricultural activity, so the resulting <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a> are major commodities. Main crops include <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beets" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar beets">sugar beets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Potatoes">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegetables" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetables">vegetables</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a>. As the prices of imported <a href="/wiki/Agrichemicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Agrichemicals">agrichemicals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> are so high, much farming is being done by hand and by horse, as it was generations ago. Agricultural processing is a key component of the industrial economy as well as one of the most attractive sectors for foreign investment. </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is rich in mineral resources but has negligible <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> reserves; it imports petroleum and gas. Among its mineral reserves are substantial deposits of <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antimony" title="Antimony">antimony</a>, and other valuable metals. <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">Metallurgy</a> is an important industry, and the government hopes to attract foreign investment in this field. The government has actively encouraged foreign involvement in extracting and processing gold from the <a href="/wiki/Kumtor_Gold_Mine" title="Kumtor Gold Mine">Kumtor Gold Mine</a> and other regions. The country's plentiful water resources and mountainous terrain enable it to produce and export large quantities of <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric energy">hydroelectric energy</a>. </p>
      <p>The principal exports are nonferrous metals and minerals, woollen goods and other agricultural products, electric energy and certain engineering goods. Imports include petroleum and natural gas, ferrous metals, chemicals, most machinery, wood and paper products, some foods and some construction materials. Its leading trade partners include Germany, Russia, China, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>. After Beijing launched the Belt and Road Initiative (BRI) in 2013, China has expanded its economic presence and initiated a number of sizable infrastructure projects in Kyrgyzstan.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In regards to telecommunication infrastructure, Kyrgyz Republic ranks last in Central Asia in the World Economic Forum's Network Readiness Index (NRI) â an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. Kyrgyz Republic ranked number 118 overall in the 2014 NRI ranking, unchanged from 2013 (see <a href="/wiki/Networked_Readiness_Index" title="Networked Readiness Index">Networked Readiness Index</a>). </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is ranked 78th among countries for economic freedom by the Heritage Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The COVID-19 pandemic is expected to have a significant negative impact on the Kyrgyz economy that is reliant on services, remittances and natural resources. As a result, in order to mitigate the economic shock and preserve much of the development progress achieved in recent years the World Bank will provide support by financing several projects in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg/220px-Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg/330px-Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg/440px-Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Issyk-Kulmeer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Southern shore of <a href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Issyk Kul Lake">Issyk Kul Lake</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Yssykkoel-lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Yssykkoel-lake.jpg/220px-Yssykkoel-lake.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Yssykkoel-lake.jpg/330px-Yssykkoel-lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Yssykkoel-lake.jpg/440px-Yssykkoel-lake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="525"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Yssykkoel-lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Issyk Kul Lake
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Tourism in Kyrgyzstan">Tourism in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>One of the most popular tourist destination points in Kyrgyzstan is the lake <a href="/wiki/Issyk-Kul" title="Issyk-Kul">Issyk-Kul</a>. Numerous hotels, resorts and boarding houses are located along its northern shore. The most popular beach zones are in the city of <a href="/wiki/Cholpon-Ata" title="Cholpon-Ata">Cholpon-Ata</a> and the settlements nearby, such as Kara-Oi (Dolinka), Bosteri and Korumdy. The number of tourists visiting the lake was more than a million a year in 2006 and 2007. However, due to the economic and political instability in the region, the number has declined in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The headquarters of the Kyrgyz Academy of Sciences is located in Bishkek, where several research institutes are located. Kyrgyz researchers are developing useful technologies based on natural products, such as heavy metal remediation for purifying waste water.<sup id="cite_ref-Yurishcheva_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yurishcheva-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG/350px-Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG" decoding="async" width="350" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG/525px-Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG/700px-Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Kirghizistan.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a> showing Kyrgyzstan's age distribution (2005).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png/350px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png/525px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png/700px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1028"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D0%B7%D0%B0_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population density of Kyrgyzstan, 2015<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Demographics of Kyrgyzstan">Demographics of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan's population is estimated at 6,586,600 in August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-census_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-91">[91]</a></sup> Of those, 34.4% are under the age of 15 and 6.2% are over 65. The country is <a href="/wiki/Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural">rural</a>: only about one-third of the population live in urban areas. The average <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> is 25 people per km<sup>2</sup>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The nation's largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> people, who comprise 73.3% of the population. Other ethnic groups include <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (5.6%) concentrated in the north and <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> (14.6%) living in the south. Small but noticeable minorities include <a href="/wiki/Dungans" class="mw-redirect" title="Dungans">Dungans</a> (1.1%), <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyghur people">Uyghurs</a> (1.1%), <a href="/wiki/T%C4%81jik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="TÄjik people">Tajiks</a> (1.1%), <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakhs</a> (0.7%), and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (0.5%) and other smaller ethnic minorities (1.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-population_by_nationality_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population_by_nationality-3">[3]</a></sup> The country has over 80 ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Kyrgyz have historically been semi-<a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> herders, living in round tents called <a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">yurts</a> and tending <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yak" class="mw-redirect" title="Yak">yaks</a>. This nomadic tradition continues to function seasonally (see <a href="/wiki/Transhumance" title="Transhumance">transhumance</a>) as herding families return to the high mountain pasture (or <i>jailoo</i>) in the summer. The sedentary Uzbeks and Tajiks traditionally have farmed lower-lying irrigated land in the <a href="/wiki/Fergana_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Fergana valley">Fergana valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kyrgyzstan has undergone a pronounced change in its ethnic composition since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spo_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spo-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spoo_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spoo-96">[96]</a></sup> The percentage of ethnic Kyrgyz has increased from around 50% in 1979 to over 70% in 2013, while the percentage of ethnic groups, such as Russians, Ukrainians, Germans and Tatars dropped from 35% to about 7%.<sup id="cite_ref-census_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-91">[91]</a></sup> Since 1991, a large number of <a href="/wiki/Germans_in_Kyrgyzstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Germans in Kyrgyzstan">Germans</a>, who in 1989 numbered 101,000 persons, have emigrated to Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Languages of Kyrgyzstan">Languages of Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a> is the state language of Kyrgyzstan. <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> is additionally an official language. Kyrgyzstan is one of four former Soviet republics to have Russian as an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>. After the division of the Soviet Union into countries, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a> was adopted as the "state language" of Kyrgyzstan in 1991. Kyrgyzstan adopted Russian as an "official language" in 1997. The languages have different legal status. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> language of the <a href="/wiki/Kipchak_languages" title="Kipchak languages">Kipchak</a> branch, closely related to <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karakalpak_language" title="Karakalpak language">Karakalpak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nogay_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nogay language">Nogay Tatar</a>. It was written in the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">Arabic alphabet</a> until the twentieth century. <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin script</a> was introduced and adopted in 1928, and was subsequently replaced on Stalin's orders by <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script#Kyrgyz" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic script</a> in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> 4.1 million people spoke Kyrgyz as native or second language and 2.5 million spoke Russian as native or second language. <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a> is the second most common native language with 700,000 native speakers. </p>
      <p>Many business and political affairs are carried out in Russian. Until recently, Kyrgyz remained a language spoken at home and was rarely used during meetings or other events. However, most parliamentary meetings today are conducted in Kyrgyz, with simultaneous interpretation available for those not speaking Kyrgyz. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Kyrgyzstan</th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Islam</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:88%; overflow: hidden;">
             â
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">88%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Russian Orthodox Church</td>

            <div style="background:blue; width:9%; overflow: hidden;">
             â
            </div></td>

          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">other</td>

            <div style="background:grey; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">
             â

          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Religion in Kyrgyzstan">Religion in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg/220px-Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg/330px-Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg/440px-Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karakol-Dungan-Mosque-Exterior-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Karakol#Dungan_mosque" title="Karakol">Karakol Dungan Mosque</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the dominant religion of Kyrgyzstan. The CIA World Factbook estimates that as of 2017, 90% of the population is Muslim, with the majority being <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>; 7% are Christian, including 3% <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodoxy</a>, and the remainder are other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-18">[18]</a></sup> A 2009 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> report indicated 86.3% of Kyrgyzstan's population adhering to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The great majority of Muslims are Sunni, adhering to the <a href="/wiki/Hanafi" title="Hanafi">Hanafi school</a> of thought,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> although a 2012 Pew survey report showed that only 23% of respondents to a questionnaire chose to identify themselves as Sunni, with 64% volunteering that they were "just a Muslim".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> There are a few <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> Muslims, though unrecognised by the country.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During Soviet times, <a href="/wiki/State_atheism" title="State atheism">state atheism</a> was encouraged. Today, however, Kyrgyzstan is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>, although Islam has exerted a growing influence in politics.<sup id="cite_ref-isn_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isn-108">[108]</a></sup> For instance, there has been an attempt to arrange for officials to travel on <i><a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">hajj</a></i> (the pilgrimage to <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>) under a tax-free arrangement. </p>
      <p>While <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Islam in Kyrgyzstan">Islam in Kyrgyzstan</a> is more of a cultural background than a devout daily practice for many, public figures have expressed support for restoring religious values. For example, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">ombudsman</a> Tursunbay Bakir-Ulu noted, "In this era of independence, it is not surprising that there has been a return to spiritual roots not only in Kyrgyzstan, but also in other post-communist republics. It would be immoral to develop a market-based society without an ethical dimension."<sup id="cite_ref-isn_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isn-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bishkek_church_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bishkek_church_01.jpg/170px-Bishkek_church_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bishkek_church_01.jpg/255px-Bishkek_church_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bishkek_church_01.jpg/340px-Bishkek_church_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1932" data-file-height="2576"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bishkek_church_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bishkek <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Bermet_Akayeva" title="Bermet Akayeva">Bermet Akayeva</a>, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Askar_Akayev" title="Askar Akayev">Askar Akayev</a>, the former President of Kyrgyzstan, stated during a July 2007 interview that Islam is increasingly taking root across the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-EurasiaNet_Kyrgyzstan_Time_to_Ponder_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurasiaNet_Kyrgyzstan_Time_to_Ponder-109">[109]</a></sup> She emphasized that many <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> have recently been built and that the Kyrgyz are increasingly devoting themselves to Islam, which she noted was "not a bad thing in itself. It keeps our society more moral, cleaner."<sup id="cite_ref-EurasiaNet_Kyrgyzstan_Time_to_Ponder_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurasiaNet_Kyrgyzstan_Time_to_Ponder-109">[109]</a></sup> There is a contemporary <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> order present which adheres to a somewhat different form of Islam than the orthodox Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg/220px-Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg/330px-Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg/440px-Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_under_construction_in_Kyrgyzstan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mosque under construction in Kyrgyzstan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The other faiths practiced in Kyrgyzstan include <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">Ukrainian Orthodox</a> versions of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, practiced primarily by <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> respectively. A community of 5000 to 10,000 Jehovah's Witnesses gather in both Kirghiz- and Russian-speaking congregations, as well as some Chinese- and Turkish-speaking groups.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> A small minority of ethnic Germans are also Christian, mostly <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran Church">Lutheran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anabaptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anabaptist">Anabaptist</a> as well as a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> community of approximately 600.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A few <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">Animistic</a> traditions survive, as do influences from <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> such as the tying of <a href="/wiki/Prayer_flag" title="Prayer flag">prayer flags</a> onto sacred trees, though some view this practice rooted within <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> There are also a small number of <a href="/wiki/Bukharian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Bukharian Jews">Bukharian Jews</a> living in Kyrgyzstan, but during the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> most fled to other countries, mainly the United States and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. In addition, there is a small community of <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a>, who fled to the country from eastern Europe during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 6 November 2008, the Kyrgyzstan parliament unanimously passed a law increasing the minimum number of adherents for recognizing a religion from 10 to 200. It also outlawed "aggressive action aimed at <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">proselytism</a>", and banned religious activity in schools and all activity by unregistered organizations. It was signed by President <a href="/wiki/Kurmanbek_Bakiyev" title="Kurmanbek Bakiyev">Kurmanbek Bakiyev</a> on 12 January 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There have been several reported police raids against peaceful minority religious meetings,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> as well as reports of officials planting false evidence,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> but also some court decisions in favour of religious minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Culture of Kyrgyzstan">Culture of Kyrgyzstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_cuisine" title="Kyrgyz cuisine">Kyrgyz cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg/220px-Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg/330px-Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg/440px-Kyrgyz_Musicians_in_Karakol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="592"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrgyz_Manaschi,_Karakol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Kyrgyz_Manaschi%2C_Karakol.jpg/170px-Kyrgyz_Manaschi%2C_Karakol.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Kyrgyz_Manaschi%2C_Karakol.jpg/255px-Kyrgyz_Manaschi%2C_Karakol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Kyrgyz_Manaschi%2C_Karakol.jpg/340px-Kyrgyz_Manaschi%2C_Karakol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="394" data-file-height="523"></a>

         </div>A traditional Kyrgyz <i>manaschi</i> performing part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Manas" title="Epic of Manas">Epic of Manas</a></i> at a yurt camp in <a href="/wiki/Karakol" title="Karakol">Karakol</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Manas_(epic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Manas (epic)">Manas</a></i>, an <a href="/wiki/Epic_poem" class="mw-redirect" title="Epic poem">epic poem</a></li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Komuz" title="Komuz">Komuz</a></i>, a three-stringed lute</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Tush_kyiz" title="Tush kyiz">Tush kyiz</a></i>, large, elaborately embroidered wall hangings</li> 
       <li><i>Shirdak</i>, flat cushions made in shadow-pairs<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Other <a href="/wiki/Textiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Textiles">textiles</a>, especially made from <a href="/wiki/Felt" title="Felt">felt</a></li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Ala_kachuu" title="Ala kachuu">Ala kachuu</a></i>, "bride kidnapping", traditional form of marriage in Kyrgyzstan</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Falconry" title="Falconry">Falconry</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._(3968888530).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._%283968888530%29.jpg/220px-Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._%283968888530%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._%283968888530%29.jpg/330px-Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._%283968888530%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._%283968888530%29.jpg/440px-Ishenbek_and_Berkut_scout_for_prey._%283968888530%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

         </div><a href="/wiki/Hunting_with_eagles" title="Hunting with eagles">Hunting with an eagle</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Illegal, but still practiced, is the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Bride_kidnapping" title="Bride kidnapping">bride kidnapping</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> It is debatable whether bride kidnapping is actually traditional. Some of the confusion may stem from the fact that <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">arranged marriages</a> were traditional, and one of the ways to escape an arranged marriage was to arrange a consensual "kidnapping."<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flag">Flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 40-rayed yellow sun in the center of <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Kyrgyzstan" title="Flag of Kyrgyzstan">the national flag</a> represent the 40 tribes that once made up the entirety of Kyrgyz culture before the intervention of Russia during the rise of the Soviet Union. The lines inside the sun represent the crown or tÃ¼ndÃ¼k (Kyrgyz ÑÒ¯Ð½Ð´Ò¯Ðº) of a yurt, a symbol replicated in many facets of Kyrgyz architecture. The red portion of the flag represents peace and openness of Kyrgyzstan. </p>
      <p>Under Soviet rule and before 1992, it had the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Flag of the Soviet Union">flag of the Soviet Union</a> with two big blue stripes and a white thin stripe in the middle. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Public holidays in Kyrgyzstan">Public holidays in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In addition to celebrating the <a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a> each 1 January, the Kyrgyz observe the traditional New Year festival <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a> on the vernal equinox. This spring holiday is celebrated with feasts and festivities such as the horse game <a href="/wiki/Buzkashi" title="Buzkashi">Ulak Tartish</a>. </p>
      <p>This is the list of public holidays in Kyrgyzstan: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>1 January â New Year's Day</li> 
       <li>7 January â Orthodox Christmas</li> 
       <li>23 February â Fatherland Defender's Day</li> 
       <li>8 March â Women's Day</li> 
       <li>21â23 March â <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nooruz Mairamy</a>, Persian New Year (spring festival)</li> 
       <li>7 April â Day of National Revolution</li> 
       <li>1 May â Labor Day</li> 
       <li>5 May â Constitution Day</li> 
       <li>8 May â Remembrance Day</li> 
       <li>9 May â <a href="/wiki/Victory_Day_(9_May)" title="Victory Day (9 May)">Victory Day</a></li> 
       <li>31 August â Independence Day</li> 
       <li>7â8 November â Days of History and Commemoration of Ancestors</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Two additional Muslim holidays <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid-al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eid-al-Fitr (page does not exist)">Orozo Ayt</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Eid-al-Adha" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid-al-Adha">Qurman (or Qurban) Ayt</a></i> are defined by the lunar calendar. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Rugby union in Kyrgyzstan">Rugby union in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG/220px-Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG/330px-Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG/440px-Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bandy_2012._KYR_-_JPN.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bandy: Kyrgyzstan in red against Japan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Kyrgyzstan. The official governing body is the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Kyrgyz_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Federation of Kyrgyz Republic">Football Federation of Kyrgyz Republic</a>, which was founded in 1992, after the split of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. It administers the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan_national_football_team" title="Kyrgyzstan national football team">Kyrgyzstan national football team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">Wrestling</a> is also very popular. In the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Summer Olympic Games">2008 Summer Olympic Games</a>, two athletes from Kyrgyzstan won medals in <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_wrestling" title="Greco-Roman wrestling">Greco-Roman wrestling</a>: <a href="/wiki/Kanatbek_Begaliev" title="Kanatbek Begaliev">Kanatbek Begaliev</a> (silver) and <a href="/wiki/Ruslan_Tyumenbayev" title="Ruslan Tyumenbayev">Ruslan Tyumenbayev</a> (bronze).<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a> was not as popular in Kyrgyzstan until the first <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan_Championship_(ice_hockey)" title="Kyrgyzstan Championship (ice hockey)">Ice Hockey Championship</a> was organized in 2009. In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Kyrgyzstan men's national ice hockey team">Kyrgyzstan men's national ice hockey team</a> won <a href="/wiki/2011_Asian_Winter_Games" title="2011 Asian Winter Games">2011 Asian Winter Games</a> Premier Division dominating in all six games with six wins. It was the first major international event that Kyrgyzstan's ice hockey team took part in.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The Kyrgyzstan men's ice hockey team joined the <a href="/wiki/IIHF" class="mw-redirect" title="IIHF">IIHF</a> in July 2011. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">Bandy</a> is becoming increasingly popular in the country. The Kyrgyz national team took Kyrgyzstan's first medal at the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Winter_Games" title="Asian Winter Games">Asian Winter Games</a>, when they captured the bronze. They played in the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Bandy World Championship 2012">Bandy World Championship 2012</a>, their first appearance in that tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Martial Arts: <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Shevchenko_(fighter)" title="Valentina Shevchenko (fighter)">Valentina Shevchenko</a> is a Kyrgyzstaniâ<a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peruvian</a> professional mixed martial artist who competes in the <a href="/wiki/Flyweight_(MMA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flyweight (MMA)">women's flyweight</a> division of the <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">Ultimate Fighting Championship</a> (UFC), where she is the current <a href="/wiki/UFC_Women%27s_Flyweight_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="UFC Women's Flyweight Championship">Women's Flyweight champion</a>. </p>
      <p>Boxing: <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Bivol" title="Dmitry Bivol">Dmitry Bivol</a> is a Kyrgyzstani Professional Boxer from <a href="/wiki/Tokmok" title="Tokmok">Tokmok</a>, who competes in the Light Heavyweight Division. Since 2017, he has held the <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Association" title="World Boxing Association">World Boxing Association</a> <a href="/wiki/Light_Heavyweight" class="mw-redirect" title="Light Heavyweight">Light Heavyweight</a> Title. As of August 2019, Bivol is ranked as the world's best active light-heavyweight by the Transnational Boxing Rankings Board and BoxRec, and third by The <a href="/wiki/Ring_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring Magazine">Ring Magazine</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan%27s_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyrgyzstan's national basketball team">Kyrgyzstan's national basketball team</a> had its best performance at the official <a href="/wiki/1995_Asian_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1995 Asian Basketball Championship">1995 Asian Basketball Championship</a> where the team surprisingly finished ahead of favorites such as <a href="/wiki/Iran_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Iran national basketball team">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Philippines men's national basketball team">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordan national basketball team">Jordan</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Horse_riding">Horse riding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Horse riding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The traditional national sports reflect the importance of <a href="/wiki/Horse_riding" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse riding">horse riding</a> in Kyrgyz culture. </p>
      <p>Very popular, as in all of Central Asia, is <i><a href="/wiki/Buzkashi" title="Buzkashi">Ulak Tartysh</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Team_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Team sports">team game</a> resembling a cross between <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> in which two teams of riders wrestle for possession of the headless carcass of a goat, which they attempt to deliver across the opposition's goal line, or into the opposition's goal: a big tub or a circle marked on the ground. </p>
      <p>Other popular games on horseback include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i>At Chabysh</i> â a long-distance horse race, sometimes over a distance of more than 50&nbsp;km</li> 
       <li><i>Jumby Atmai</i> â a large bar of precious metal (the "jumby") is tied to a pole by a thread and contestants attempt to break the thread by shooting at it, while at a gallop</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Kyz_Kuumai" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyz Kuumai">Kyz Kuumai</a></i> â a man chases a girl in order to win a kiss from her, while she gallops away; if he is not successful she may in turn chase him and attempt to beat him with her "kamchi" (horsewhip)</li> 
       <li><i>Oodarysh</i> â two contestants wrestle on horseback, each attempting to be the first to throw the other from his horse</li> 
       <li><i>Tyin Emmei</i> â picking up a coin from the ground at full gallop</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Education in Kyrgyzstan">Education in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The school system in Kyrgyzstan includes primary (grades 1 to 4, some schools have optional 0 grade), secondary (grades 5 to 9) and high (grades 10 to 11) divisions within one school.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Children are usually accepted to primary schools at the age of 6 or 7. It is required that every child finishes 9 grades of school and receives a certificate of completion. Grades 10â11 are optional, but it is necessary to complete them to graduate and receive a state-accredited school diploma. To graduate, a student must complete the 11-year school course and pass 4 mandatory state exams in writing, maths, history and a foreign language. </p>
      <p>There are 77 public schools in Bishkek (capital city) and more than 200 in the rest of the country. There are 55 higher educational institutions and universities in Kyrgyzstan, out of which 37 are state institutions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2016, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Asia" title="University of Central Asia">University of Central Asia</a> was launched in Naryn, Kyrgyzstan.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan is home to 1,066 libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_the_Kyrgyz_Republic" title="National Library of the Kyrgyz Republic">National Library of the Kyrgyz Republic</a> is the oldest library in the country, which was established in 1934. Kyrgyz Libraries are working towards expanding access to communities, evident in projects such as the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh_VIP_Treaty" title="Marrakesh VIP Treaty">Marrakesh VIP Treaty</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">Open access</a> Portal.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg/220px-E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg/330px-E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg/440px-E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:E8102-Bishkek-West-Bus-Terminal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bishkek West Bus Terminal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kyrgyzstan" title="Transport in Kyrgyzstan">Transport in Kyrgyzstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Transport in Kyrgyzstan is severely constrained by the country's alpine topography. Roads have to snake up steep valleys, cross passes of 3,000 metres (9,800&nbsp;ft) altitude and more, and are subject to frequent mudslides and snow avalanches. Winter travel is close to impossible in many of the more remote and high-altitude regions. </p>
      <p>Additional problems come from the fact that many roads and railway lines built during the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> period are today intersected by international boundaries, requiring time-consuming border formalities to cross where they are not completely closed. <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">Horses</a> are still a much-used transport option, especially in more rural areas; Kyrgyzstan's road infrastructure is not extensive, so horses are able to reach locations that motor vehicles cannot, and they do not require expensive, imported <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>At the end of the Soviet period there were about 50 airports and airstrips in Kyrgyzstan, many of them built primarily to serve military purposes in this border region so close to China. Only a few of them remain in service today. The <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan_Air_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Kyrgyzstan Air Company">Kyrgyzstan Air Company</a> provides air transport to China, Russia, and other local countries. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Manas_International_Airport" title="Manas International Airport">Manas International Airport</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> is the main international airport, with services to Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urumqi" class="mw-redirect" title="Urumqi">Urumqi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Osh_Airport" title="Osh Airport">Osh Airport</a> is the main air terminal in the south of the country, with daily connections to Bishkek, and services to Moscow, Krasnoyarsk, Almaty and more international places.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jalal-Abad_Airport" title="Jalal-Abad Airport">Jalal-Abad Airport</a> is linked to Bishkek by daily flights. The national flag carrier, Kyrgyzstan, operates flights on <a href="/wiki/BAe-146" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe-146">BAe-146</a> aircraft. During the summer months, a weekly flight links Jalal-Abad with the Issyk-Kul Region.</li> 
       <li>Other facilities built during the Soviet era are either closed down, used only occasionally or restricted to military use (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Kant_Air_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Kant Air Base">Kant Air Base</a> near Bishkek, which is used by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Air_Force" title="Russian Air Force">Russian Air Force</a>).</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banned_airline_status">Banned airline status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Banned airline status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Kyrgyzstan appears on the European Union's <a href="/wiki/List_of_air_carriers_banned_in_the_European_Union" title="List of air carriers banned in the European Union">list of prohibited countries for the certification of airlines</a>. This means that no airline that is registered in Kyrgyzstan may operate services of any kind within the European Union, due to safety standards that fail to meet European regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> No EU airline has flights to Kyrgyzstan (as of 2020). Travel between the European Union and Kyrgyzstan includes changing aircraft, most often in Moscow or Istanbul. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Chuy_Valley" title="Chuy Valley">Chuy Valley</a> in the north and the <a href="/wiki/Ferghana_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferghana valley">Ferghana valley</a> in the south were endpoints of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>'s rail system in Central Asia. Following the emergence of independent post-Soviet states, the rail lines which were built without regard for administrative boundaries have been cut by borders, and traffic is therefore severely curtailed. The small bits of rail lines within Kyrgyzstan, about 370&nbsp;km (230&nbsp;mi) (1,520&nbsp;mm (59.8&nbsp;in) broad gauge) in total, have little economic value in the absence of the former bulk traffic over long distances to and from such centres as <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, and the cities of Russia. </p>
      <p>There are vague plans about extending rail lines from <a href="/wiki/Balykchy" title="Balykchy">Balykchy</a> in the north and/or from <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a> in the south into China, but the cost of construction would be enormous. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_links_with_adjacent_countries">Rail links with adjacent countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Rail links with adjacent countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kazakhstan" title="Transport in Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> â yes â <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> branch â same gauge</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Uzbekistan" title="Transport in Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> â yes â <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a> branch â same gauge</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Tajikistan" title="Transport in Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> â no â same gauge</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport in the People's Republic of China">China</a> â no â <a href="/wiki/Break_of_gauge" title="Break of gauge">Break of gauge</a> 1524&nbsp;mm/1435&nbsp;mm</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg/220px-Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg/330px-Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg/440px-Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5023" data-file-height="3139"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Osh_03-2016_img07_Gapar_Aitiev_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Street scene in <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With support from the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, a major road linking the north and southwest from <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> to <a href="/wiki/Osh" title="Osh">Osh</a> has recently been completed. This considerably eases communication between the two major population centres of the countryâthe <a href="/wiki/Chuy_Valley" title="Chuy Valley">Chuy Valley</a> in the north and the <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana Valley</a> in the South. An offshoot of this road branches off across a 3,500 meter <a href="/wiki/Mountain_pass" title="Mountain pass">pass</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Talas_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Talas Valley">Talas Valley</a> in the northwest. Plans are now being formulated to build a major road from Osh into China. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i>total:</i> 34,000&nbsp;km (21,127&nbsp;mi) (including 140&nbsp;km (87&nbsp;mi) of expressways)</li> 
       <li><i>paved:</i> 22,600&nbsp;km (14,043&nbsp;mi) (includes some all-weather gravel-surfaced roads)</li> 
       <li><i>unpaved:</i> 7,700&nbsp;km (4,785&nbsp;mi) (these roads are made of unstabilized earth and are difficult to negotiate in wet weather) (1990)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports_and_harbours">Ports and harbours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyrgyzstan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Ports and harbours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Balykchy" title="Balykchy">Balykchy</a> (Ysyk-Kol or Rybach'ye) on Issyk Kul Lake.</li>
      </ul>

        <li><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.press.umich.edu/titleDetailDesc.do?id=17240">Politics of Language in the Ex-Soviet Muslim States: Azerbaijan, Uzbekistan, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan, Turkmenistan and Tajikistan</a></i> by Jacob M. Landau and Barbara Kellner-Heinkele. Ann Arbor, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan_Press" title="University of Michigan Press">University of Michigan Press</a>, 2001. 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-472-11226-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-472-11226-5">978-0-472-11226-5</a></li> 
        <li><i>Kyrgyzstan: Traditions of Nomads</i> by V. Kadyrov, Rarity Ltd., Bishkek, 2005. 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9967-424-42-7" title="Special:BookSources/9967-424-42-7">9967-424-42-7</a></li> 
        <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://admissions.kg/cities/">Cities in Kyrgyzstan</a></li>
